At least one ``authorization response header`` is added to the client request, or is used for\\n88:   // altering another client request header.\\n89:   //\\n90:   bool clear_route_cache = 6;\\n91: \\n92:   // Sets the HTTP status that is returned to the client when the authorization server returns an error\\n93:   // or cannot be reached. The default status is HTTP 403 Forbidden.\\n94:   type.v3.HttpStatus status_on_error = 7;\\n95: \\n96:   // When this is set to true, the filter will check the :ref:`ext_authz response\\n97:   // <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.auth.v3.CheckResponse>` for invalid header &\\n98:   // query parameter mutations. Works with both HTTP and GRPC clients.\\n246:   //\\n247:   // When this is set to true, header values are not sanitized. Headers with the same key will also\\n248:   // not be combined into a single, comma-separated header.\\n249:   // Requests to GRPC services will populate the field\\n250:   // :ref:`header_map<envoy_v3_api_field_service.auth.v3.AttributeContext.HttpRequest.header_map>`.\\n251:   // Requests to HTTP services will be constructed with the unsanitized header values and preserved\\n252:   // multi-line headers with the same key.\\n253:   //\\n254:   // If this field is set to false, header values will be sanitized, with any non-UTF-8-compliant\\n255:   // bytes replaced with '!'.
